No Price Increase for French Concession Water 270

Thanks to the Metering System

The American Evening Post reports that after the Shanghai Waterworks Company in the International Settlement was authorized by the Municipal Council to increase prices, rumors spread that the French Concession Water Company would also raise prices. This morning (the 9th), a reporter visited an official of the French Concession Water and Electricity Company, who claimed that these rumors were unfounded. The French Concession uses a metering system, so customers conserve water. Therefore, the current prices can be maintained unless the company's financial situation worsens significantly. Even if a price increase becomes necessary in the future, it will be minimal to avoid unnecessary hardship for the public. In their opinion, the Shanghai Waterworks Company could have avoided the 25% price increase if it had adopted a metering system years ago. Metering is the only effective way to eliminate waste.

Japanese Empress Vessel Invites All Circles to Visit Yesterday 276

Today Inaugurates Maiden Voyage to Canada

The newly built Japanese Empress vessel of Changxing Company, having sailed from England for the first time, arrived in Shanghai yesterday. As the vessel's displacement is 39,000 tons, its length is 666 feet 5 inches, its width is 83 feet 5 inches, and its draft is even deeper, it was anchored at the Wusong mouth without entering the Huangpu River. The vessel's first arrival in Shanghai saw the company issue a large number of invitations to various circles to visit. Three small steamers were specially dispatched to welcome visitors at the Customs Wharf to board the vessel. At 2:00 PM, it left Shanghai, and at 3:30 PM, there were over a thousand people visiting the ship, including many Westerners. The vessel's construction is excellent, divided into seven decks with four types of passenger accommodations: first, second, third, and steerage. Inside the ship, there are gardens, swimming pools, smoking rooms, dining halls, grand lounges, dance halls, and more. The beauty of the arrangement is almost comparable to palace halls. The structure is made of granite paired with colored carvings. The floors are covered with colored rubber carpets. Radio, music, movies, and other facilities are all available. Upon entering the ship, passengers feel as if they are entering a grand hotel in a bustling city, without feeling the hardships of sea travel. The first-class cabins are very sophisticated, with double and single rooms, some attached with bathrooms. The ship also has a ticket office of the Canadian Railway Company to facilitate passengers' train connections. The vessel's speed is extremely high, usually capable of traveling over 21 nautical miles per hour. The engine is extremely powerful, using the latest type of fuel oil. With three smokestacks, it takes only twelve days to reach Vancouver from Shanghai, including stops in Japan. Crossing the Pacific to North America in a direct route would only take nine days. Yesterday, those who visited the vessel all expressed admiration, confirming it as the fastest and largest excellent mail steamer in the Pacific, worthy of the name "Empress." However, when tea and refreshments were served to the visitors after boarding the ship yesterday afternoon, the order was very chaotic, almost turning into a scramble for food. If guests could be entertained according to their status, it would be more universal and the spectacle would be slightly more organized, without the situation of Western guests receiving special treatment while many Chinese guests did not receive refreshments, as happened yesterday. This reporter returned by steamer.

Page 16

It is already 7:30 PM in Shanghai. The Japanese Empress is scheduled to inaugurate its maiden voyage to Canada today.

Liu Jin Sends Hunan Guild Relief 279

Liu Jin, a Hunanese who served as a junior officer in the military, has been living in seclusion in Changsha since his retirement. He, along with his mother, sister-in-law, wife, children, and others, totaling nine people, are extremely impoverished. At the end of last month, the Communist Party ravaged Changsha, causing an unprecedented catastrophe. Liu, supporting the elderly and leading the young, fled with his family, enduring countless hardships before arriving at Pukou. His elderly mother died en route, and his elder sister-in-law committed suicide in Pukou. Beset by disasters, Liu sought help everywhere, but ultimately, due to being unfamiliar with the people and the place, his appeals went unanswered. In desperation, he attempted suicide by throwing himself into the Huangpu River. Fortunately, he was rescued and sent to the Water Police Station. A suicide note was found on his person, its words so mournful as to be unbearable to read. The original text was published in yesterday's newspaper. After questioning by the police station, it was learned that a fellow townsman, Liu Jusheng, runs the Liu Ju Ji Paper Shop at No. 44 Chungi Lane, Qipan Street, Shanghai. That evening, a detective accompanied Liu to search for him. Upon arriving at the shop, Liu was not present. A clerk, He Meisheng, came out and, upon learning the purpose, made excuses that the owner was away and declined to take responsibility for providing relief. Detective Cheng Yongnian and others, aware that Liu's younger sister-in-law, wife, and children, totaling six people, were still stranded in Pukou without anyone to provide for them, and that Liu was bearing a heavy burden, decided that abruptly releasing him would inevitably lead him to attempt suicide again due to lack of money to return to Pukou. Therefore, they immediately hired a car to send him to the Hunan Guild Relief Center at Xieqiao, where he was taken in and provided with funds to be sent back to Pukou for further planning.

Record of the Trial of an Indian Gun Trafficking Case 281

Zhang Yuting Identifies the Indian From Among The Crowd

Monk Singh Cannot Deny The Crime And Finally Confesses

On the fourth day of this month, Zhang Yuting, a detective from the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's water patrol team, discovered that an Indian man named Monk Singh was carrying 302 restricted bullets near the Wanyu Wharf in the South City. He was immediately taken back to the team. After a preliminary trial by Chief Xu, the person and evidence were submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning and investigation. After the case occurred, the public security bureau of the public concession learned that the case was related to Indian. They immediately sent detective to the bureau to request that the Indian be brought back for interrogation. The bureau approved to let the Indian be taken away and later sent to the British Consulate General. It was heard that the British consul took the case seriously, so the court was opened some days ago to trial the case. The court first summoned more than twenty Indians to mix Monk Singh with them, make them to line up at the court and ordered the detective Zhang Yuting to identify Monk Singh. Many of the Indians were in the public gallery, so when Zhang was asked to identify Monk Singh in public, Zhang was able to identify Monk Singh. Zhang said that on the day he patrolled Wanyu Wharf, he saw an Indian Monk Singh carrying a red cloth package which looked suspicious so he went forward to check him out, but Monk Singh wanted to resist. Then he saw that he had a gun, so Monk Singh dare not to resist. When he checked his package, he found 302 bullets. Then Zhang brought Monk Singh back to the police team. Monk Singh’s initial testimony was denial, but after repeated questioning, he confessed that the bullets were being taken somewhere to be sold. He said that there was a man named A Si who lived in Qichang Zhai, Pudong. A Si runs a used goods business and sells bullets with him. The court sent Officer Ross and Zhang Yuting to Qichang Zhai to arrest A Si. However, A Si had already heard about this and ran away. It was found that Monk Singh had worked as a guard at the Jianghai Customs Ammunition Depot, resulting in the theft of over 20,000 bullets from the depot. Therefore, the bullets found were from the depot. At 10am of yesterday, the court was opened to trial the case. Monk Singh bowed his head and said nothing when he was asked questions. The court declared that there were solid evidences to prove that Monk Singh trafficked illegal goods and ordered that Monk Singh be detained and the verdict would be announced some day.

Son Dies, Mother Swallows Opium to Join Him in Death 282

Yan Chen, an old woman from Suzhou who lived at No. 376 Changbang Road, had a daughter-in-law named Yan Wu, only 21 years old. She had been married for not long and had a son whom both the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law cherished. Unexpectedly, the son did not live long and died on the 27th of last month. One was heartbroken over the grandson, and the other felt a deep maternal love, crying incessantly. Wu was even more grief-stricken and developed thoughts of ending her life, exhibiting suicidal tendencies. Her mother-in-law gently dissuaded her, so she remained alive. At 6:00 AM the day before yesterday, Wu went out in tears. When her mother-in-law asked where she was going, she replied that she was going to the market to buy vegetables, so her mother-in-law did not suspect anything. However, Wu took the opportunity to purchase opium paste and returned home, secretly consuming it. Before long, the poison took effect, causing abdominal pain. Chen still thought it was indigestion and sent her to Baolong Hospital. The diagnosis was poisoning, and it was beyond salvation. She died at 8:00 AM. The Xinzha Police Station, upon receiving the report, dispatched detectives to carry the body to the forensic examination office on Fielun Road. Opium Used to Treat Illness Leads to Death 283

Chen Huang Dies of Stomach Disease

Chen Huang, a young woman from Ningbo, was 24 years old. This spring, due to the poor living conditions in her hometown, she came to Shanghai intending to find work as a female worker. After a long time, she was introduced by a fellow townsman, Mr. A, to work as a servant in the Lin residence in Wusong, where she was considered diligent and frugal. However, she had a history of stomach problems that recurred intermittently, causing severe pain, insomnia, and vomiting. She suffered greatly. The day before yesterday, her old illness recurred, causing severe stomach pain. Upon hearing someone say that taking a small amount of opium could relieve the pain, she went to a certain place to purchase a few coins' worth of opium. Lacking a lamp and pipe, she swallowed the raw opium. Unexpectedly, within a few hours, the poison took effect, causing her to groan in bed. The employer immediately took her to the hospital twice for treatment, but the poison had entered her intestines, making it impossible to save her. She gradually died. The local police station has ordered a guarantor to report the matter to the local court for examination. One version states that she intentionally took the poison.

Case of Accusation of Wife Insulting Elders and Request for Divorce Awaits Verdict 284

Xu Longsheng, a villager from the 30th Bao 3rd Tu of this county, has hired lawyer Chen Wenxiang to sue his wife, Xu Zhang, in the local court for insulting his elders and requesting a divorce. After repeated summonses, no resolution was reached, and he was instructed to reconcile outside of court. The day before yesterday, Judge Tong Shengli opened the court again to hear the case. As the witnesses were not complete, he was instructed to invite Yao Zixiang for a retrial. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong again opened the court. After both parties briefly presented their cases, the official ordered Yao Zixiang to be brought to the case to provide testimony. Yao Zixiang, age 34, farmer, stated: "I am the maternal uncle of the plaintiff. Xu Longsheng came to me to say that the husband and wife were quarreling, and I advised him to be more tolerant. I don't know the specifics." The interrogator understood the situation and invited Prosecutor Zhao to the court to present his opinion. The interrogator then ruled that the case's arguments were concluded and that the verdict would be announced on the 12th. He then adjourned the court.

Remarried Woman Firmly Requests Divorce 285

Claims to Be Unloved by Husband for Being "Too Big"

A woman named Lu Fubao has filed a petition with the local court requesting the annulment of her marriage contract. The main points of her petition are that, due to having no one to rely on after her husband's death, she remarried Wu Caizhang through an introduction. A marriage contract was drawn up. However, after living together, Wu Caizhang pawned her clothes and jewelry and subjected her to abuse. The defendant, Wu Caizhang, also submitted a defense, stating that due to a lack of someone to take care of the household, he had only married the plaintiff on March 6th of this year through a matchmaker, paying a dowry of 200 yuan. Barely a month after she entered the home, he noticed that her actions were strange, often going out and not returning. He advised her to stay home, but she ignored him. Now she suddenly petitions for the annulment of the marriage contract. However, the defendant requests that the losses he has suffered not be compensated and that they continue living together. This case was publicly heard the day before yesterday without resolution, and was adjourned for further testimony. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Tong Shengli specially opened the eighth court for a retrial. Both the plaintiff, defendant, and the defendant's witnesses - Wu Chen (defendant's mother), Wang Wu (defendant's sister), Wang Erkang (defendant's brother-in-law, i.e., Wang Wu's husband) - and the plaintiff's lawyer, Chen Jinrong, all arrived at the court as summoned. First, Wang Erkang testified, stating that he was 28 years old, from Yuyao, residing at No. 39 Shengsheng Lane, Baoshan Road, Zhabei, and working on the Ningbo train in Shanghai. "The defendant, Wu Caizhang, is my brother-in-law." (Question) "What kind of business does the defendant do, and how much does he earn per month?" (Answer) "He (referring to Wu Caizhang) works at a dance hall on Sichuan Road, earning a monthly salary of over 30 yuan." (Question) "How can he make ends meet with such a small salary?" (Answer) "My mother-in-law, Wu Chen, is supported by me. Moreover, he has income from small side jobs, which is enough to manage." (Question) "Do you know why they want to separate?" (Answer) "The defendant's business usually ends around 2:00 AM, after which he returns home. Now, because foreign sailors and others go there to have fun, he often has to stay until dawn to close up and go home. The plaintiff does not understand this and mistakenly suspects that the defendant has a lover or is smoking opium, which leads to arguments." Next, Wu Chen testified, stating that she was 55 years old, from Zhenhai, and currently living at her son-in-law's home. (Question) "Why don't you live with your son and daughter-in-law, but instead live with your son-in-law?" (Answer) "Because my son-in-law has no parents, I often live with him." (Question) "Are your son and daughter-in-law harmonious with each other?" (Answer) "They are harmonious." Wang Wu testified, stating that she was 19 years old. (Question) "Have you ever been to your brother's house?" (Answer) "No, I have never been there because I was sick after giving birth." (Question) "Can you mediate to prevent them from separating?" (Answer) "I cannot persuade them. I have tried to persuade them before, but they would not listen." Lu Fubao testified, requesting permission to dissolve the marriage contract. She also stated that after living with the defendant, she exchanged her gold bracelet for 57.40 yuan and pawned her pearl bracelet for 50 yuan, all to pay off the defendant's debts. She also pawned her pearl circle to buy a Western suit for the defendant. Initially, they treated me very well, but now that they see that my jewelry has been tricked away, the three of them (referring to the defendant and his mother and sister) are of one mind in abusing me. I really cannot bear the hardship." The official said, "You are not a child of three or two years old, it cannot be so easy." (Answer) "Everything is true. Moreover, the defendant has never liked big women." (Note: The plaintiff was wearing a short white summer cloth shirt with blue flower trim around the cuffs, trousers of roasted fragrance cloud gauze, flesh-colored silk stockings, and sky-blue flower satin shoes. She had short hair and a very obese body, but her appearance was quite good and her speech was eloquent. The defendant was wearing a white glued cloth Zhongshan suit.) The official ordered the defendant, Wu Caizhang, to be brought to the case and testified that he did not want to separate. The plaintiff's statements were all false. The official then invited Prosecutor Xu Heling to the court to express his opinion. After deliberation, he considered the arguments concluded and scheduled the sentencing for the 12th of this month.

Husband and Concubine Separated Due to Opium 286

Zhu Jinsheng and Sun Meiyu

Zhu Jinsheng, a bean and wheat merchant residing in Dou City Street in the South City, took a Suzhou woman named Sun Meiyu as his concubine several years ago. She was 35 years old. He rented a house for her in the South City and provided all expenses on a monthly basis. For several years, they lived in peace. Recently, however, Meiyu developed liver disease, which led to her smoking opium. As a result, her expenses increased significantly, and disagreements arose repeatedly over the use of money. Jinsheng, finding his repeated advice ineffective, filed a complaint with the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office, accusing Sun Meiyu of smoking opium. The court arrested Meiyu and sentenced her to a fine of 60 yuan and two months of detention. However, Meiyu appealed and requested to be released on bail. While Meiyu was in detention, Jinsheng went to Meiyu's room to collect all her belongings and found 19 pawn tickets, some for 160 yuan and others for over 10 yuan. After Meiyu was released on bail, she repeatedly negotiated with Jinsheng. After repeated mediation by friends of both parties, they agreed to sever their family relationship. The agreed conditions were: (1) Jinsheng would pay Meiyu 1,500 yuan as future living expenses; (2) all items in the room would be taken away by Meiyu; (3) all utensils in the parlor would belong to Jinsheng. After the above conditions were agreed upon, an agreement was drawn up at lawyer Jin Yu's office, proving that they would forever sever their family relationship. However, the court appeal was scheduled to be heard yesterday, and the plaintiff has requested permission to withdraw the self-accusation portion. The husband-concubine lawsuit has thus come to an end.

The Dredging Bureau previously ordered a shallow-water dredger from the Jiangnan Shipyard. The blueprints were all drawn by the Dredging Bureau. The newest dredger is particularly beneficial for inland river dredging work. It is said that the cost is approximately 300,000 taels of silver. The dredger has already been manufactured and launched some days ago. The shipyard sent a letter to the Dredging Bureau requesting that they send personnel for acceptance. It is said that the Dredging Bureau immediately sent Chinese engineers Huang Yan and Xia Ruifu to the shipyard for acceptance. According to the shipyard, the dredger can dredge 2,000 cubic meters of mud per day working eight hours on inland rivers, making it the newest type. It is also said that the dredger will be used to undertake dredging work on the Suzhou River.

Where Has Jing Yuan Gone?

Jing Heyun, a Shandong native residing at No. 35 Zhaofeng Lane, Zhongshan Road, Republican New Road, Zhabei, makes Tianjin trouser belts. He and his wife, Yuan, weave trouser belts together at home. The husband and wife have a good relationship. Yuan used to recognize Old Wang, a neighbor in Qingjiang, as her godmother. Flower Gambling in the French Concession Repeatedly Raided 290

The French police have recently been strictly cracking down on flower gambling in the concession. The day before yesterday, it was discovered that Wang Changsheng at No. 4 Xingchang Lane, Zilaihuo Street, Wang Zhang, a woman at No. 2 Ruifu Lane on the same street, and Wang A'er at No. 45 Yuxing Street, Xiaodongmen, were privately setting up flower gambling parlors to entice people to gamble, violating the prohibition. The police were ordered to raid the premises, confiscating flower gambling evidence and silver coins, and bring them to the police station. Yesterday, they were brought to court for investigation. First, the head of the police reported the situation to the court and presented the evidence. The defendants admitted to privately setting up flower gambling parlors, violating the prohibition. Chinese and Western officials sentenced the three defendants to a fine of 80 yuan each and confiscated the flower gambling documents for destruction. According to the French court's precedent, the first offense of flower gambling is punishable by a fine of 50 yuan. Since the day before yesterday, the fine has been increased by 30 yuan to deter gamblers from illegal activities.

Stolen Goods Found in Police Officer's Home 291

Lin Houzhen Detained for Two Weeks

Wang A'da, residing on the fourth floor of No. 8 Hongyun Lane, Huage Road in the French Concession, reported to the French police the day before yesterday that he had left home on business some days ago and that thieves had broken into his room and stolen twenty pieces of clothing. When the merchant returned home and learned of the theft, he knew that the stolen goods were in the home of Lin Houzhen, a Chinese police officer No. 388 who lives at No. 222 on the same road, and immediately went to demand them back. However, Lin arbitrarily demanded a bribe. The police chief, upon receiving the report, was furious that a police officer would dare to engage in such illegal activities. He immediately dismissed him and ordered detectives to arrest Lin and his relatives - Lin's wife, Jiang; and Lin's brother, Tiecai - and detain them, and to recover the stolen goods, which were missing five pieces of clothing. Yesterday, they were sent to the French court for investigation. First, the plaintiff complained about the theft and stated that he had already agreed to give a reward of 80 yuan, but the defendant refused, so he reported the matter to the police for investigation. Lin Houzhen testified that some days ago, a citizen was returning home when he passed the entrance of Hongyun Lane No. 8 and saw a thief carrying clothes trying to escape. When he saw the citizen coming, he abandoned the stolen goods and fled. At that time, the citizen asked if anyone knew who the clothes belonged to, but everyone said they didn't know, so the citizen temporarily took them home and informed the lane manager to let the owner know that they could come and retrieve them. Later, when the plaintiff came to retrieve them, the citizen was not at home and did not dare to demand a bribe. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Lin Jiang testified that some days ago, her husband brought a package of clothes home. When she asked where they came from, he said he had found them and told her to send them to Lin Tiecai for safekeeping. That was the truth. Lin Tiecai testified that the stolen goods were sent by his sister-in-law for safekeeping and that he did not know they were stolen. Judge Zhu sentenced Lin Houzhen to two weeks of detention as a warning and Lin Jiang and Lin Tiecai to seven days of detention with a one-year suspended sentence. The stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff.

Restaurant Worker Dies Suddenly on Bicycle 292

Examination Confirms Death Due to Cerebral Anemia

Zhong Tiao, a Japanese national in Shanghai, runs a Japanese restaurant at No. 471 Zhaopu Road and employs a Chinese worker named Teng Fuming to assist with everything. Around 7:00 PM the day before yesterday, Teng rode a bicycle to deliver meals to a customer's home. After finishing the delivery, he rode his bicycle back to the restaurant. When he reached Wusong Road, he suddenly fell off the bicycle. He got up and tried to get back on, but he fell again and his face turned pale. He suddenly died. A rickshaw puller, Chen Bingyuan from Haimen, passed by and, seeing the situation, immediately reported it to the police. The police arrived and carried the deceased to the forensic examination office. Yesterday, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the Special District Court, along with a clerk and bailiffs, arrived to examine the body. According to the forensic examination, the deceased suffered from cerebral anemia, which could cause death in severe cases. Zhong Tiao stated that the deceased was delivering meals that day and that he did not know the cause of death. Prosecutor Guo asked if he could take care of the body on behalf of the family until his family arrived, but Zhong Tiao, disregarding the relationship between employer and worker, refused, saying that the family had been notified by telegram and would arrive in Shanghai today or tomorrow to claim the body. Helpless, Guo ordered that the body be temporarily kept at the forensic examination office. If his family had not arrived to claim the body by 2:00 PM that afternoon, it would be handed over to the Pushan Villa for safekeeping until the family claimed it.

Homeless Boy Wandering 295

Trafficked to Xiamen

Then Rescued to Shanghai

Gu Gendao, an eleven-year-old boy from Gaohang Township, Pudong, had a father named Fo Fo. His father passed away when he was seven, and his mother died when he was nine. Orphaned and alone, his uncle, a Buddhist monk named Lu Heshang, took pity on him and, out of familial kindness, took him in. Unexpectedly, Lu also passed away the following year (last year). Consequently, the aunt saw the boy as an omen of bad luck and mistreated him severely, often depriving him of food. Dissatisfied, one day she put Gu on the Donggou ferry to Shanghai, abandoning him on the Nanjing Road wharf. After purchasing her ticket, she returned on the same ferry. Friendless, Gu's cries were in vain. However, being resourceful, he wandered along the docks of Pudong, begging for food from Chinese and foreign merchant ships during the day, and sleeping on ships docked in Shanghai at night, becoming a dockside beggar (commonly known as "Xiao San"). His hardships are self-evident. When the Taikoo Company's Xiamen-bound "Nanchang" ship docked at the Taikoo Wharf overnight on its last trip to Shanghai, Gu, exhausted, was again sleeping on the ship. A certain Second Steward of the ship, seeing an opportunity to make a huge profit by luring young boys and girls to Xiamen for sale, saw Gu alone on the ship and conceived an illegal scheme. He lured Gu into a cabin and confined him. After the ship set sail, Xin Rongquan, the ship's oiling foreman, and his deputy, Luo Xingfa, discovered the plan and realized what the Second Steward was up to. However, being out at sea, they refrained from confronting him. They planned to hand over the Second Steward and Gu to the local police in Xiamen for investigation. Unexpectedly, before the ship docked in Xiamen, the Second Steward escaped alone on a sampan towards the mountains, evading punishment. Unable to do anything, Xin and Luo left the boy on the ship and returned to Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon, after arriving in Shanghai, Luo took Gu to the Water Police Station. After learning the details, the station telegraphed the General Women and Children's Relief Association, and investigator Lin was dispatched to take Gu into the association's care and education.

Thousand-Layer Lotus at the Zhejiang-Shaoxing Guild Hall 296

The host of the Zhejiang-Shaoxing Guild Hall in Houjia Bang, Lao Beimen (Old North Gate) of this city, has always loved growing lotuses. Every summer, the courtyards inside and outside the main hall (housing the Xuan Tan deity) of the guild hall are filled with lotus flowers. This year, two unusual lotus flowers bloomed, one bright red and the other snow-white. The red one lacks lotus seeds in its heart and has multiple layers of petals, called a "Thousand-Layer Lotus." The white one has lotus seeds in the center, but its petals differ from ordinary lotuses. The most remarkable thing is that ordinary lotus flowers drop their petals within one to four days of blooming, but these thousand-layer lotus flowers have been blooming for three weeks and remain fresh and lovely. As a result, many people have been visiting to admire them daily, and many have approached the host of the guild hall with cameras, seeking to photograph these lotus flowers.

The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Chen to three weeks of imprisonment as a warning.

Discussion on Raising Funds for Dredging Yutang River 300

Yutang, located in a crucial area of the county, is the most important river in the county, spanning four districts: one, two, three, and six. Its eastern mouth connects to the Huangpu River, passing through towns such as Tangwan, Beiqiao, and Maqiao. Transportation and irrigation depend on this river. In recent years, it has become increasingly silted, causing inconvenience to farmers, merchants, and industrialists. Therefore, dredging the river cannot be delayed. The associations in each district along the river have formed a dredging committee to raise funds. The proposed method of collecting funds from farmland was not approved by the county government. Now, the chairman of the committee, Yang Fulin, believing that this matter concerns the county's waterway transportation, has scheduled a meeting on the twelfth of this month to discuss funding solutions, hoping to resolve the issue. It is said that the estimated cost is approximately ten thousand yuan.

Weather Report 308

The Xujiahui Observatory issued the following weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday: The skies will be mostly cloudy along the coast, with a risk of showers. The Yangtze River basin will be sunny. The coastal areas of the East China Sea will be overcast. The northeasterly winds will strengthen over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea. The weather around the Ryukyu Islands is extremely bad, as two hurricanes have merged into one and are moving northeast or north. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 94.5 degrees and the lowest was 74.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 93.2 degrees and the lowest was 74.8 degrees.

Free Talk

Laugh It Off 309

— Hai Ke

Painter A: My paintings have improved a lot lately. The other day, I drew a silver dollar on the ground in front of my house, and two beggars fought to pick it up, even breaking their heads open.

Painter B: That's nothing. Yesterday, I drew a large ham on a stone step, and a hungry dog came to eat it, eating half of the stone step without realizing it was fake.

Car Salesman: This car only costs 3,500 taels. In this era of cheap silver, it couldn't be cheaper.

Customer: Is everything included in the car?

Car Salesman: The four lamps on the car are not included.

Customer: How can that be? Even in the pictures in the book, the lamps are drawn together.

Car Salesman: It's not like that. Look, there's also a beautiful woman drawn in the car. Do you think that for 3,500 taels, we should include a beautiful woman?

A: Alas, I could have been a great tycoon, but those foreign machines ruined me. There's no hope of getting rich anymore.

B: What do foreign machines have to do with you?

A: I was an accountant at a foreign hotel, and the extra income was great. But that cunning foreign owner started using some kind of machine to collect accounts, and I was tied hand and foot and couldn't do anything.

Anecdotes of Mr. Sheng Shengfu 310

— Qing Song Ju Shi

Mr. Sheng Shengfu Bingwei, a superintendent of education in Jiangxi and Sichuan, enjoyed a reputation for his accomplishments. After the revolution, he retired to the mountains and forests, maintaining a leisurely life for twenty years. Now, he has suddenly passed away. The passing of an elder statesman is deeply regrettable. My friend, whose relative is married to Mr. Sheng's son, knows much about Mr. Sheng's childhood and later life. Here are some of the highlights:

A Famous Teacher in Distress; A Successful Father's Rise. The father of Sheng Shengfu had meager savings from his business in the market, but he hoped his son would become famous, a sentiment rare in the world. He hired a famous scholar as a teacher and personally attended to the scholar's needs with great sincerity. The scholar was grateful for the hospitality and taught with all his heart. One day, the scholar took leave for some reason, and the young Sheng played truant. He had forgotten much of his lessons. The teacher, with a sincere desire to help, threw the teaching stick at Sheng, hitting him between the eyebrows. Sheng felt great pain and fainted. The scholar was deeply embarrassed and fled during the confusion. He met Sheng's father on the way, who was carrying a teapot and asked what had happened. The scholar was flustered and ashamed, unable to speak. Only after the father repeatedly insisted did he stammer and tell the whole story, weeping, "I have no face to meet my host now." The father, upon hearing this, looked relieved and urged the scholar to return, saying, "My son is unworthy and cannot listen to the teacher's instructions and fulfill his father's wishes. He should be punished. I will never hold any resentment." The scholar was touched by his sincerity and cried, promising to repay him. He agreed to return with him. From then on, Sheng, after enduring the pain, resolved to study diligently.

A Heroic Woman. Sheng passed the imperial examinations at a young age, earning a great reputation for his literary talent. The people in his hometown competed to choose him as their son-in-law. He married a daughter of a scholar named XX, who was bright-eyed and beautiful. The young couple was so deeply in love that they could not bear to be separated for even a moment. During the year when he was to take the imperial examinations in the capital, he returned home several times. His parents, seeing his infatuation, persuaded his wife to feign a quarrel to break his heart and strengthen his resolve. Sheng remained calm and wished to spend his life in the gentle embrace of his wife. The wife, unable to do otherwise, comforted him earnestly, "With your prime years, you should not abandon your ambition. I would be ashamed to be friends with a common man. Now that you have passed the exam and are starting on a journey of ten thousand miles, you should not be trapped by sentimental feelings. How can you fulfill the painstaking efforts of your parents who wish for their son's success? Strive hard and do not be reluctant to leave." Upon hearing this, Sheng shook off his sleeves and set off for the capital. In the gengchen year, he and Zhu Fuxuan from Haiyan and Huang Shao from Rui'an passed the palace examination and were admitted to the Hanlin Academy, known as the three famous scholars of eastern Zhejiang, admired by the literary world. This was based on the enlightenment of a famous teacher. When drinking water, we should remember the source. It was due to the father's respect for the teacher, but it was also due to the wife's influence.

News of Lightning Strike 311

— Hong Xiao

Last month, there was a case of lightning striking a person to death during a storm in this city. A daughter died and her mother was injured. Superstitious people tried to combine the story, inventing a rumor that the daughter had evil intentions to harm her mother, so she was struck by lightning. Furthermore, since the mother did not see the tragedy of her daughter being struck by lightning, the thunder deity sent another bolt of lightning, suspending the mother in mid-air, so that she would not witness it. This far-fetched story has been published in various newspapers, and many people know about it. It is not necessary to repeat it. Now, let me tell you a more certain case of a lightning strike as retribution, so that those who invented the story of the mother being injured and the daughter dying may be shocked and speechless. The event took place in Yangxiang Town, Liyang. There were two Zhang brothers, Fukang and Fulin, who were farmers. Their family was wealthy, and the two brothers were very close. They had not yet divided the family property. Fukang had no heir, while Fulin had a son who was already twenty years old. Therefore, he was passive, but he never stopped yearning for an heir to the family. Last fall, his wife, Wang, miraculously became pregnant. Fukang was overjoyed, but Fulin's wife was very angry, worrying that if Wang had a son, her son would not be able to inherit the entire family property. When winter came, Fukang suddenly fell ill and died. Wang was grief-stricken, but she was happy that she had a child in her womb. However, Fulin's wife was relieved. Time passed quickly. In May of this year, Wang gave birth. Fulin's wife had long planned to poison her. She didn't call a midwife and volunteered to deliver the baby. If it was a girl, she would accept it, but if it was a boy, she would find a way to kill it. Wang was unaware and thought her sister-in-law cared for her. Unexpectedly, when the baby was born, it was a boy. Fulin's wife, without hesitation, ripped off the baby's genitals while Wang was asleep. The baby died and was buried in the suburbs. Wang was old and weak. She woke up the next day and thought everything was normal. Fulin's wife falsely claimed that the baby was born weak and died immediately. Wang didn't suspect anything and blamed herself for being unlucky. A month later, disaster struck. On the sixth day of the sixth month (the date may be incorrect), the weather was clear and people were suffering from the heat. Suddenly, the wind and clouds changed, and it rained heavily with thunder and lightning. Fulin's wife was struck by lightning and killed in the storm. Her death was gruesome. After the rain stopped, people from far and near came to see. Her entire body was charred and contracted. There seemed to be words on her back, but no one could recognize them. Everyone was amazed. Fulin was so frightened that he was pale. He thought it must be because his wife had murdered his brother's son and offended the gods. He was afraid that he would not be spared, so he confessed his wife's crime to reduce his guilt. The people then realized that the deceased must have done evil in her life, and they believed that there were gods. I have heard many stories of people being struck by lightning, but none have been as clear as this. Is there really a thunder deity? In reality, lightning is caused by the friction of electricity and air. The truth is clear. The old legend of the thunder deity is nonsense. Wang Chong of the Han Dynasty refuted its fallacy. There is a saying in Lunheng: "The image of thunder drawn by painters is like a series of drums. They also draw a person like a strong man, calling him the thunder god, with a drum in his left hand and a hammer in his right hand. The people believe it, and none doubt it." Even the false image of Fuyuan. Although the incident of the daughter's death and the mother's injury is not worth inventing, how could the death of Fulin's wife be so miraculous?

Little Experience on Taking the Train 312

— VB

If it is not early when you arrive at the station, after buying your ticket, you can go directly to the front carriage, where there must still be empty seats waiting for you. With the psychology of a traveler, everyone is greedy for convenience, and everyone likes to squeeze into the carriages at the back. They are unwilling to walk a few more steps to find a spacious place. If we know this trick, we will naturally not be afraid of not having a good place.

When taking the train, you should not be polite. Don't be afraid that the carriages are full of people. I should take a seat on other people with a fearless spirit. Those who are sleeping will naturally be restless and will have to get up and let me take it. If you ask politely and carefully for a long time, the result is that people ignore you and get bored.

Also, if you already have a seat, don't give it to others. Don't feel sorry for others who can't find a seat. If you give people a little space, they will take advantage of you. Even your own space will be squeezed out. This is practical experience.

You can't take the Shanghai-Nanjing night train now, because in this hot weather, everyone is greedy for coolness and has switched to taking the night train, so the night train is very crowded. There is not even a place to stand. There are fewer passengers on the day train. The quietest is the Shanghai-Nanjing-Hangzhou train at 4:00 PM in the afternoon. It is the most comfortable.

Buying newspapers on the train is twice as expensive as outside the station. If we are preparing to take a train far away, we can buy several copies of newspapers and cigarettes and food before entering the station.

The price of tea on the train now has an unwritten price. Regardless of the distance, Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou are two jiao and two fen for third class, four jiao or six jiao for second class, and one yuan for first class. The sleeping car is charged separately, about two yuan is enough. Also, the third class on the Jinpu Line does not have tea, so you must bring your own thermos. The price of tea in the first and second classes is about the same as on the Shanghai-Nanjing Line.

If the porters at the station carry things below Nanjing, they will still follow the station rules and charge a few cents per piece. If you arrive at the Nanjing station, the porters will charge you an indefinite amount. Three jiao is also one piece, two jiao is also one piece. Moreover, according to the porters' rules, even a small hatbox must be counted as one piece of luggage. The Jinpu Line is about the same. The porters in Tianjin and the dockworkers in Tianjin are very skilled at charging. They dare to ask you for one yuan to carry a piece of luggage from the shore to the ship. If you don't give him six or seven mao, you won't be able to leave. People who go out should know this.

Eastern Travel Impressions (28) 313

— Qian Hua

(24) The Ryuta Maru's Return Voyage

The three most popular things in modern Japanese society are: firstly, mahjong; secondly, Chinese cuisine; and thirdly, dancing. The most famous Chinese restaurants in Tokyo include a few establishments such as the China First Building, the Beijing Pavilion, and the Shanghai Pavilion. The China First Building, specializing in Cantonese cuisine, has been established for decades and enjoys an excellent reputation. It has built its own five-story building with painted rafters and carved beams, decorated in an extremely luxurious manner, resembling a palace in Beijing. Ordinary swallow's nest dishes range from 35 to 60 Japanese yen per table. Japanese people often use Chinese cuisine for grand banquets, and women, in particular, consider it an honor to taste its flavors. The initial capital of the China First Building was only a few hundred yen, but it has now accumulated to hundreds of thousands. The restaurant business definitely occupies a considerable position among overseas Chinese. Mahjong became popular two years ago and has flourished especially this summer. The mahjong tiles are all imported from China, exquisitely carved, and sell for 30 to 40 Japanese yen per set in Japan. There are over a thousand mahjong clubs in Tokyo, each with several exquisitely decorated small rooms serving as mahjong parlors. After joining a game, each player pays one Japanese yen per four rounds, using chips to count wins and losses, not money. Its nature is entirely a game, distinct from gambling. As for the fee distribution method, the biggest loser pays six "jiao" (tenths of a yen), followed by three "jiao," then two "jiao," and the biggest winner plays for free. The clubs provide some fruit and refreshments for the guests, so the clubs' earnings are actually minimal. The owner's purpose is not to make petty profits but to gather like-minded individuals to study. Chinese students often go to the mahjong clubs with four or five friends on weekends and holidays for mahjong battles, still secretly calculating wins and losses in money. This trend has recently spread to upper-middle-class Japanese families as well, with significant sums changing hands in a mahjong game. Japanese people devote great effort to mahjong research, using scientific methods to create various strategies, with multiple mahjong magazines as the crystallization of their research. Society also distinguishes mahjong skill levels into nine grades, similar to the grading system in Go, with the first grade being the most basic and the ninth grade being the highest. Even mahjong terminology is now being changed to use Chinese pronunciation. It is predicted that after a few more years of research by the Japanese, they may be able to compete with Chinese mahjong masters. After the closing ceremony of the Games, the reporter originally planned to do some sightseeing in famous Japanese scenic spots, but because the Nippon Yusen Kaisha's newly built giant ship, the Ryuta Maru, happened to be sailing from Kobe to Shanghai on June 4th, this was a rare maiden voyage opportunity. Moreover, the Chinese athletes' delegation was also returning home on the same ship, so I wouldn't feel lonely during the journey. Thus, I left Tokyo hurriedly on the evening of June 3rd and arrived in Kobe on the morning of the 4th, immediately boarding the ship to rest. Zeng Junyanhua came to bid farewell. After spending ten days together, we parted ways, and I couldn't help but feel melancholy. At exactly 12 noon, the Ryuta Maru cast off from the port. The Ryuta Maru, with a displacement of over 10,000 tons, is perfectly equipped and even better than the Shanghai Maru. The journey was smooth and the sailing was extremely comfortable. I repeatedly met and talked with Zhang Boling, Zhao Jinqing, Lin Kanghou, and others. Zhao said that the Japanese people's construction capabilities are indeed admirable, but they imitate Europe and America in everything, which feels excessive. For example, if someone can eat two bowls of rice, they insist on eating three, which leads to indigestion and is detrimental to health. Japan's current situation is similar, while our country suffers from being either excessive or insufficient, both being detrimental, he said. I also discussed the issue of Japanese women cutting their hair with Japanese friends on the ship. Japan imitates Europe and America in everything else, but it uniquely resists the worldwide trend of women cutting their hair. During my twenty days in Tokyo, I only saw a dozen or so women with short hair on the streets, which is quite remarkable. It is said that Japanese society spares no effort in maintaining the old morality of women, so even with the development of women's professions today and the ability of women to live independently, women's rights have made no progress. Preserving hair is one way to maintain the old morality, and they vigorously promote the beauty of long hair while attacking women who cut their hair, even regarding them as being on par with prostitutes. Thus, among Japanese women, you can hardly find one or two out of a hundred who cut their hair. Due to financial reasons, most of the athletes' delegation stayed in third-class cabins, but they ate meals from the second-class menu. Returning home after defeat, they no longer had the courage they once possessed. On the morning of the 6th, at 10 am, amidst the sound of firecrackers, we safely arrived at the Waibaidu Bridge wharf. The reporter's rambling notes also come to an end. I sincerely tell our Chinese athletes that failure is the mother of success, and we should encourage ourselves even more and continue to work hard. We will see the flag of the Republic of China flying high in the tenth Games, achieving great victories in all fields.

Eastern Travel Correspondence (17) 314

— Wu Xiaohou

(5) New Small Parks: Fifty-one small parks, each approximately 3,000 square meters, have been newly built in the earthquake-stricken area. The total cost for the establishment of trees, flower beds, plazas, sports equipment, and children's play facilities is approximately 14,341,196 yen.

(6) Waste Disposal Facilities: There are 27 waste treatment plants, 2 waste collection stations, and 4 factories. The equipment expenses are approximately 1.85 million yen.

(7) Central Wholesale Market Construction: Due to the destruction of city streets and houses after the Great Kanto Earthquake, large open spaces were available for the construction of the central wholesale market. In addition to the main market, two branch markets were established in Kanda and Koto. The construction costs are approximately 16.5 million yen.

(8) Elementary School Construction: The reconstruction of 116 municipal elementary schools requires each school to be built to a standard of 24 classes and a floor area of 4,554 square meters. The original wooden buildings are being replaced with reinforced concrete (similar to what we in China call cement and steel) three-story buildings. The total construction cost is approximately 40,939,096 yen.

(9) Social Welfare Facilities: The social welfare projects include 12 job placement centers, 10 nurseries and children's health consultation centers, 4 women's vocational training centers, 10 public canteens, 10 simple lodging facilities, 7 pawnshops, and 10 bathhouses. The cost of all the facilities is approximately 4,525,000 yen.

(10) Municipal Hospital Construction: The five municipal hospitals are all two-story reinforced concrete buildings. The total cost is approximately 3.1 million yen.

(11) Rapid Water Supply and Reconstruction: The construction of the new Tokyo Tamagawa Aqueduct, the Yodobashi Water Purification Plant, and the reconstruction of the earthquake-damaged city water supply system, as well as the completion of the Murayamashita Reservoir in the city's water supply expansion project and the Wada-hori Shinjuku line water pipe laying project, totaled approximately 10 million yen.

(12) Electrical Facilities: The new construction and improvement of earthquake-damaged tracks, wires, vehicles, transformer substations, and all related equipment totaled approximately 30,420,000 yen.

The total cost of the twelve city reconstruction projects is 350,402,828 yen. Combined with the government facility expenses of 336,987,465 yen and the Tokyo Prefecture facility expenses of 22,004,036 yen, the total is 709,394,329 yen. In just over seven years, the government and local authorities have cooperated in reconstruction, sparing no expense and dedicating all their efforts. As a result, the city's facilities are now more well-planned and advanced than before the Great Kanto Earthquake.

Gold Market Continues to Decline

Fluctuations Not Large, Continuing to Show Weakness 315

Yesterday, the gold market continued its sluggish trend, but the movement was moderate, with only minor ups and downs of three to two taels. The exchange rate was tight, with banks slightly taking in, and brokers uncertain about supply and demand. Firms like Hengxing, Zhifengyong, and Yong were eager to buy, while Yifengyong, Taikangrun, and others were selling. Large bars remained unchanged, with more sellers appearing each day. The opening price was low, but Hengxing and others scrambled to buy, pushing the price up to the 80 tael mark. However, when the exchange rate eased at noon, firms were inclined to sell, and the price was pushed down by two or three taels. Disappointing results led to weakening sentiment. The final price was 77 taels plus some change.

Yarn Market Weakened Due to Multiple Blows 326

No Significant Impact on Actual Sales

The decline in the yarn market was due to a consistent sharp drop in overseas cotton yarn markets, leading to weakened sentiment. However, actual sales were not significantly impacted. The Guangdong brokers were still strong, and the Niuzhuang brokers were also active, so the market could still maintain its current state temporarily. The situation was still stable, but some, seeing the unfavorable global situation, slightly sold short. The yarn market is currently relatively strong due to good demand for existing yarn and is unlikely to experience a sharp fall. The future is unpredictable.

Moderate Decline in Man-Made Fiber Market 327

The man-made fiber market opened lower in the morning, following the decline in overseas cotton, and sentiment was fearful, with long positions closing out. The price for each month fell by eight or nine "qian" to one tael. In the afternoon, hearing that actual sales were good, the market slightly stabilized, and the price for each month fell by two or three "qian." The total transaction volume for the day was 16,050 bales. Shenxin sold the most at 2,200 bales, followed by Lichang at 1,000 bales. Gongtai, Yu Kang, Shenchang, Hengyi, Dachang, Chengtian, Changmao, Shenji, and Yuantai Changfeng sold between 350 bales and 1,500 bales. Yiyu bought the most at 1,150 bales, followed by Heshen, Yu Da, Daji, Taisheng, Kang Hanfeng, Xiesheng, Tianlong, Yongfeng, and Senkang, selling between 350 bales and 1,200 bales. The closing prices for the man-made fiber market are recorded below:

Continued Strong Sales of Existing Yarn 328

The sales of existing yarn remained strong. The total amount of spot and futures bought by various groups for the day was 3,435 bales, with 75 bales bought by counterparts. The market fell by five "qian." The Niuzhuang group bought the most at 915 bales, followed by Guangdong at 880 bales, the interior at 325 bales, Xuzhou at 170 bales, Shantou at 510 bales, Sichuan at 40 bales, Wuhu at 45 bales, Yunnan at 120 bales, Tianjin at 355 bales, and miscellaneous groups at 80 bales.

Cotton Market Plunged by Six "Qian" 329

Devastated by Sharp Fall in American Cotton

The cotton market plunged because the American cotton government's estimates favored short positions, and the price fell by more than 60 pounds, which was unexpected by most people. Furthermore, the sharp rise in long positions the day before had led to expectations of rising American cotton prices, but the opposite happened, resulting in a more violent reaction. Selling pressure was significant, and the market was in a state of great panic. Retail investors and the Ningbo group closed out their long positions, and sellers took the opportunity to exert downward pressure. If American cotton production is over 14 million bales, the price of 12 cents is difficult to maintain. The world cotton industry is declining, and consumption has decreased sharply. 1.4 million bales from last year have not yet been sold off, so Japanese merchants have long been aiming for 11 cents. However, the local cotton market can still be temporarily stabilized due to various tightening measures.

Many Long Positions in the Domestic Cotton Market 330

The domestic cotton market opened lower in the morning, following the sharp fall in American cotton, and selling pressure increased, causing the market to decline. Many long positions closed out, falling by five "qian" each. In the afternoon, due to reports that American cotton had received rain, Ruida liquidated its holdings from the previous day, selling 14,000 bales, causing each contract month to fall by another one "qian." The total transaction volume for the day was 75,400 bales. Meiji sold the most at 10,500 bales, followed by Maoji at 9,800 bales, Ruida at 14,000 bales, Yu Da, Gongtai, Shenchang, Yongfeng, Yicheng, and Daji at between 2,500 and 1,100 bales. Yichang bought the most at 4,900 bales, followed by Yiyu at 3,500 bales, Dachang, Chengtail, Xingda, Daji, Yuan Da, Taichang, Yu Chang, Dafu, Hengyi, and Tianchang at between 2,700 and 1,100 bales. The closing prices for the domestic cotton market are recorded below:

Complete Stoppage of Existing Cotton Transactions 331

Existing cotton business has stopped. Factories have ample supply of Indian cotton and unfavorable news about American cotton, with leftover effects from the price drop, so there is no further interest. There is no information on the source.

American Cotton After the Release of Estimates 336

Unfavorable Weather… New Cotton Marketed More Smoothly… Demand Not Strong

New York, 8th—A telegram reports on the cotton market conditions for the past week, stating that before the government's cotton production estimate was released today, market prices soared due to prolonged drought and heat in the central and western cotton belts. After the government report was released, sentiment became uncertain as the estimated cotton production differed greatly from private reports. Without this report, the buying trend would have been even stronger. After the rise in grain prices, there was some cotton purchasing in the west, and banks have paid more attention to various commodities, including cotton, than before. Some sources say that timely rainfall can help cotton crops, but if the drought continues for another half month, the important cotton-growing areas in the central and western regions will have no hope of recovery. Unfavorable weather in August should stimulate active demand among traders, as it is heard that traders have not made sufficient advance preparations for the cotton they will need this season, as they did in the past.

Another report says the government's cotton production report was higher than expected, which is seen as favorable for shorts. New cotton is being marketed more smoothly, but demand is not strong. The situation in the spinning and cotton goods industries remains poor. It is heard that there has been some rain in several places in the southwest. Grain River Bottom Rice Market Declines

Zhabei 337

Yesterday, the supply from inland areas was very scarce, but sales in this area were extremely sluggish. The North Japonica market is increasingly weak because the factory and warehouse stocks are eager to sell Japonica rice, and the prices in the inland market are also trending downward. New goods are becoming increasingly available on the market, so sentiment in this area is quite soft and buying interest is very weak. Prices for high-grade, mid-grade, and low-grade rice have all fallen by 30 to 40 cents, totaling a drop of about one yuan in the past three days. However, the price of top-grade Japonica rice remains at 21 yuan. East New Japonica rice has also fallen by half a yuan, with an opening price of 20 yuan. The market outlook appears weak and thin. Stocks of late-season rice are still scarce, and there is no clear standard for the market. Sales are slow and changing, and the market trend is weakening, with transactions limited to small amounts. The situation in all sectors of the market was consistently poor throughout the day, and the overall trend may be downward.

South Shanghai 338

Very few boats arrived from the river bottoms, and sales were flat. High-priced Changshu and Wuxi machine-milled Japonica rice was rare, and medium-grade rice was also not abundant. The market was slightly weak, by a few cents. The situation in the Suzhou and Tongzhou Japonica rice market was similar, with flat and weak prices, and sellers had no possibility of raising prices. At a time when the market is declining, how could prices rise? However, fresh goods are in better demand because they are more palatable to buyers, so prices are stable. The market for late-season early rice is quiet. The price of new Japonica rice is still the same as in the Zhabei market, opening at 20 yuan. The state of sales for both white and glutinous rice is unremarkable.

Soybean Market Sentiment is Firm and Stable 339

Recently, the soybean market has been quite firm. Shipments from Dalian have been scarce. Only new soybeans from Jiujiang have been arriving continuously. Both sales in this area and purchases by customer groups are focused on high-quality goods. The market sentiment for medium-grade and lower-quality soybeans is dull, and there is a strong tendency to raise prices for higher grades. Yesterday, 4,300 packages of Jiujiang Jiqing City and other goods opened at a high price of 5 taels and 6 qian.

Inland Sales of Foreign Rice are Gradually Picking Up 340

Small Broken Rice Rises Alone by 10 Cents

Yesterday, foreign rice continued to show signs of activity, with inland brokers taking over 3,000 bags. Brokers from Hubei Province were also inquiring about small broken rice for rural villages, and prices immediately rose by 10 cents. Although the prices of other types of rice did not rise, they felt more active compared to the sluggishness of the previous days. The total market opened with over 2,000 bags of small broken rice at a price of 14 yuan and 7 jiao and 5 fen, 1,000 bags of large broken rice at 13 yuan and 7 jiao and 13 yuan per bag, and 200 bags of Min Dang rice at a price of 15 yuan and 5 fen. 500 bags of No. 1 Saigon rice were priced at 17 yuan and 7 jiao and 5 fen, and 400 bags of No. 2 rice were priced at 13 yuan and 8 jiao. 100 bags of Cover rice were priced at 14 yuan and 7 jiao and 5 fen, and 1,000 bags of Xu Ye Place brown rice were priced at 13 yuan and 5 jiao. 500 bags of small broken brown rice were priced at 11 yuan and 7 jiao and 5 fen. Brown rice and large broken rice were more active because they were being taken by inland brokers.

Reasons for the Decline in Flour Prices 341

After the flour market opened yesterday, prices for all near and distant months fell consistently. The main reason is that actual sales have been hampered by bans and foreign flour. Customer groups dare not inquire, and hoarders have no intention of inquiring because rice prices are flat and the new rice harvest is approaching. Moreover, the price of foreign flour has fallen, and smaller factories are secretly selling off their stocks, all of which are sufficient to realize the decline in the flour market. In the afternoon, there were slight improvements as some customers inquired, but in the end, this month still fell by 25 cents, September by 75 cents, October and November were unchanged, December fell by 1 cent, and January fell by 75 cents.

Futures Wheat Comes Out of the Cage and Immediately Drops by 20 to 30 Cents 342

Spot Market Appetite Turns Sluggish… More Arriving Than Being Consumed

Yesterday, after the futures wheat market opened, it was rumored that foreign flour would be discounted and a large number of Japanese and American flour shipments would arrive in China, causing the market to become flooded and prices to immediately fall by 20 to 30 cents. Although the rumor of foreign flour arriving in China could not be confirmed for Shanghai or Tianjin, the actual sales of flour were sluggish, and factories' appetite for wheat waned. The futures wheat market was ultimately unable to recover. As a result, this month fell by 2 cents, September and November fell by 1 cent, October was unchanged, and December and January each fell by 2 cents. The spot wheat market appetite turned sluggish, and more wheat was arriving than being consumed. Owners reduced prices to sell off their stocks, with 5,000 bags offered at an opening price of 4 taels and 9 qian and 7 fen for old cart wheat, 4 taels and 9 qian and 2 fen for new cart wheat, 4 taels and 6 qian and 5 fen for Shashi wheat, and 4 taels and 4 qian for Zhenjiang wheat. All prices were 30 to 50 cents lower than the previous market.

Silk, Tea, Needle Eyebrow Green Tea Sales to Europe are Thriving 343

Yesterday, both the Road and Indigenous Districts were buying needle eyebrow green tea from Yihe, Jinlong, Xiehe, and other firms without leaving any behind, and transactions were very active. Although the path for Precious Eyebrow Green Tea sales was lively, the selling prices were seen to be low by 10 to 20 taels, and the market was still difficult to consider optimistic. The Gongxi brand of White Head Tea was very scarce in the indigenous districts, and the Russian Cooperative Society's acceptance prices were especially harsh. Chinese tea merchants insisted on not selling because the quantity was not large.

White Fabric for European Sales Continues to Emerge 344

Yesterday, the foreign silk market in this area continued to be firm and prosperous. New York silk mills' futures demand has not waned, and French firms have also continued to make purchases. The current futures market sentiment is thriving. Yesterday, 150 packages of Shangzhong Shanghai white fabric were purchased by Qianli and others, and prices have generally risen.

Sugar Market, Five Blessings White Ice Sales are Particularly Good 345

Before the establishment of ice plants, sales in Shanghai were sluggish, and Xiamen factories have recently stopped production one after another, so the supply has often been unavailable. However, because the demand for Five Blessings ice is relatively broad, Xiamen factories have already prepared to start boiling, and the inventory here is also gradually becoming scarce. Yesterday, the Number Square also opened with over 100 boxes at a price of 6 taels and 7 qian per block. Few other brands opened, and as autumn sales approach, the market conditions should gradually become active.

Shanghai Market

Business News 368

The World Restaurant at the intersection of North Sichuan Road, Yokohama Bridge, and East Baoxing Road announces that it has recently observed the rise of Cantonese cuisine restaurants in Shanghai, and that their cooking is suitable for the tastes of Shanghai people. Therefore, it has specially hired famous Cantonese chefs to specialize in authentic Cantonese dishes and various famous snacks, all of which are readily available. The restaurant is opening today.

Miao Ji Department Store on North Sichuan Road announces that the company held a ninth-anniversary shopping gift lottery last month, and the lottery was drawn on the morning of the 1st of this month as scheduled. The winning numbers have also been published in Shen Xin, Shi Bao, and Shi Shi newspapers on the 2nd and 3rd of this month. However, as of yesterday, there are still twelve grand prizes that have not been claimed. In order to achieve the purpose of the gift lottery, the company is republishing the winning numbers, both claimed and unclaimed, in today's supplement of this newspaper so that those who hold the company's lottery tickets can re-check them and avoid omissions.

Maochang Optical Company on Minquan Road, west of the old North Gate, announces that since the company specially established a low-price department, the business has been booming. Now, genuine crystal glasses are being sold at reduced prices. Whether they are plano, reading, or nearsighted glasses, each pair is sold for only three yuan.

The Chaxiang Room, next to the Shanghai Grand Theatre at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Qiujiang Road, announces that the room has been established for many years and has always been known for its research into cooking techniques and its concern for hygiene. It has hired famous Cantonese chefs to skillfully prepare various foods that are delicious and affordable, and have long been praised by all walks of life. Because of the summer season, a special cold food department has been established to sell various well-made cold foods. There are too many items to list, so the customers are always full and there is a great rush to serve them.

Theater News 369

Qingtian Film Company announces that all of its staff and actors are now in Peiping engaged in the production of a martial arts romance film, "The Three Heroes of Yanjing," co-directed by the famous Shanghai directors Chen Tianzhu and Xue Hua.

Beijing Grand Theatre announces that the long-renowned Grand Theatre has recently spared no expense to completely repair and renovate all of its buildings. Both the interior and exterior of the theater have been completely renewed, and the lobby and theater are magnificent and luxurious, and very different from the old form. The film projectors and screens will also be replaced with the latest American products. This project will be completed in about half a month, and it is expected that the Grand Theatre will once again cause a sensation in Shanghai and be as grand as when it opened.

Haixing Film Company announces that its director, Mr. Dong Tianwei, emphasizes martial arts in the film "Tears of the Cold Palace Song", so he sincerely invited Mr. Zha Ruilong, a well-known strongman in the East. Everyone has long heard of Mr. Zha's brilliant boxing skills and amazing knife and gun skills. This superb skill has been tested on the screen and has been welcomed by various film merchants and audiences, who say that he is the only martial arts star in the East. Mr. Zha has been sincerely invited to be the protagonist of this film, and it is now scheduled that all the male and female actors will go to Shantou on the 13th of this month to start filming.

Wuchang Grand Theatre announces that the theater will begin showing the great production "Love, Heaven, and Grievance" by the Niao Fa Company today. The film is full of tragic and beautiful scenes that are moving everywhere, and it is more outstanding than films such as "Camellia" and "Weak Willow in a Gale." It stars the newly emerged beautiful star, Ke Mimi Maihang. The film was previously shown at the Guanglu Grand Theatre and was sold out every day. This is the second time the theater has shown it.

Medical News 370

Taihe Pharmacy at the intersection of Simalu and Shandong Road announces that the foreign-educated doctors Huang Guanying, who are hired by the pharmacy, will thoroughly examine and investigate before prescribing medicine. They will not rashly prescribe medicine unless they know the root cause of the disease. If it is necessary to use injections or acupuncture, and especially for venereal diseases, they are particularly adept at injections and other surgical procedures. Therefore, the number of patients who have been cured by them is countless. Consultation hours are from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM.

Shaonian Chinese Medicine Association in Yuqingfang, North Sichuan Road, announces that the "Verified Cases of Modern Famous Doctors" published by the association is a rare publication in the Chinese medicine field in recent years. The first two issues have sold more than 1,000 copies. Recently, in order to promote Chinese medicine, the association is distributing the publications widely at no cost. Those who request the publications can attach four cents for postage to receive one issue, or eight cents to receive two issues.

Calligraphy and Painting News 371

Danghu Hu Wuhu announces that his art name is Xie An. He is proficient in calligraphy and is skilled at formal script. He has been practicing in Shanghai for decades, and those who seek his works are numerous. He is renowned in Jilin. This autumn, he will be celebrating his mother's 90th birthday, and he is reducing his fees to help with disaster relief in order to do good deeds. It is heard that the collection points are: No. 3, Former County Chamber of Commerce, Xiaonanmen, Shanghai; Chunhua Tang, Laomalu, Nanshi; and major stationery and fan shops in Beishi.

Publishing News 372

The third issue of the "Caoye Weekly," volume 3, published by Caoye She at No. 34 Feilun Road, is published today. It contains Wang Tiehua's "Marching Song," Huang Huanruo's "Glory of the Prison," Wu Xiling's "An Old Woman's Autobiography," more than ten pieces of literary news such as "Generals," as well as "Reader's Mailbox" and "Final Words." All newspaper vendors and school gatekeepers are selling the magazine. Requests by mail should include two cents for postage.

Shanghai Beauty Society announces that the photography collection "The Essence of Beauty" by Dan Duyu has been printed and is now being bound. It is scheduled to be published on August 15. The book contains ten photos of beauties, all of which are wonderful and ethereal. The text includes Zheng Yimei's short stories and a biography of Ms. Tan Xuerong, all of which are ancient and worth reading. The deadline for pre-orders is approaching, so those who wish to pre-order the book at Renji Road, No. 35, Dachunghua Lily Company are coming in an endless stream.

(2) All businesses, film companies, theaters, calligraphers/painters, and doctors submitting manuscripts must affix a seal for verification; otherwise, we regret that the manuscript will not be published.

Shen Bao Pictorial Weekly

The Question of Sovereignty over New Antarctic Land 374

Antarctic exploration initially stemmed from the curiosity of scientists, but recently it has gradually become a matter of political interest. Since 1774, through the efforts of Cook, Weddell, Bellingshausen, Ross, Shackleton, and most recently Wilkins and Ellsworth, successive discoveries have revealed the Antarctic continent. It is known to be rich in valuable minerals such as gold, copper, coal, and diamonds. The Southern Ocean is also abundant in whales. Furthermore, it is understood that these locations can serve as air bases for global aviation. Consequently, there is no shortage of those seeking sovereignty, particularly the United Kingdom and the United States. Each claims prior discovery and names the locations after their own people, drawing worldwide attention. However, with the initial completion of naval reduction treaties, the United Kingdom is unwilling to create further disputes at this time and adopts a temporarily tolerant attitude. Nevertheless, it is foreseeable that this will become a major international issue in the future.

(1) American Welcome - German Enthusiasm 375

Edmirel Richard E. Byrd

The expedition arrived in New York on June 19. Proceeding along Broadway to City Hall, the streets were empty as people competed to welcome him. Flowers were thrown to express welcome. Admiral (X) stood in the car, frequently tipping his hat in response.

(2) The Achievements of Admiral Byrd 376

Admiral Byrd while in Antarctica. Admiral Byrd, commissioned by the American Geographical Society, flew over the North Pole for the first time on May 9, 1926. More recently, he flew over the South Pole on November 30 of last year. He is the only person to have flown over both poles.

(3) The Establishment of Little America 377

The Byrd expedition arrived in Antarctica on January 17 of last year and built a new house and a radio station on the Ross Ice Shelf. Its pen name is Little America, which can be described as a colony.

(4) Changes in the Antarctic Map 378

The Antarctic continent... Much of the land within the ice is yet to be determined. The coastline is approximately 14,000 [li] in length. Currently, only 5,000 [li] have been discovered. Present-day explorers are focused on whether the Antarctic region is a single continent, two major islands, or multiple fragmented landmasses connected by ice. The graphic indicates the location of what is called Little America.

(5) Sir Wilkins' Leisure 379

Sir Herbert Wilkins

Sir Herbert Wilkins, leader of the British polar expedition, holds a camera in the icy wilderness, taking a picture of a penguin. The knight returned home via New York on March 19.
